Khiyar al-Itiq for a Freed Mukatabah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar al-itiq for a freed mukatabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on khiyar al-itiq for a freed mukatabah, identify Imam Zufar's objection, and explain why the majority holds the option exists based on the 'illa of increase in ownership.

Core Idea
Increase in ownership, not lack of consent, is the true cause of khiyar al-itiq—so a freed mukatabah has the option.

We now turn to an intra-Hanafi dispute about khiyar al-itiq for a freed mukatabah. Imam Zufar argued that since the mukatabah consented and her dower is hers, the option should not apply. The majority Hanafi imams disagreed, focusing on the effective cause: the increase in ownership upon freedom. This lesson unpacks their reasoning and shows how Hanafi usul of 'illa determines the ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and parties
Recognize that the dispute is about whether a freed mukatabah (slave with contract of manumission) has the option (khiyar) to annul her marriage upon freedom. The majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) say yes; Imam Zufar says no.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
2
State Imam Zufar's proof
Zufar argues that the option for a regular slave woman (amah) exists because of two factors: (1) her marriage was executed without her consent, and (2) her dower belonged to her master. Since the mukatabah consented and her dower is for herself, these factors are absent, so no option.
3
Explain the Hanafi majority's response
The majority replies that a regular slave woman's consent is legally irrelevant; the true cause ('illa) of khiyar al-itiq is the increase in ownership (izdiyad al-milk) that occurs upon freedom—specifically, the husband gains an additional divorce and the woman's iddah lengthens.
Focus on the 'illa: increase in ownership, not consent or dower.
4
Apply the 'illa to the mukatabah
The same increase in ownership occurs for a freed mukatabah: before freedom her iddah is two cycles and her husband owns two divorces; after freedom these become three. Therefore, the cause exists and the option is established.
The majority uses talil (causation) rather than direct textual evidence.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: according to the majority, a freed mukatabah can annul her marriage; according to Zufar, she cannot. The majority view is mufta bihi.

Source Text

مکاتبہ نے اپنے شوہر کی اجازت سے نکاح کیا پھر آزاد ہو گئی اسے بھی اختیار ہے وكذلك المكاتبة يـعـنـى اذا تزوجت باذن مولاها ثم عتقت وقال زفر رحمه الله لاخيار لهالان العقد نفذ عليها برضاها و كان المهر لها فلا معنى لاثبات الخيار بخلاف الامة لانه لا يعتبر رضاها ولنا ان العلة ازدياد الملک وقد وجدناها فى المكاتبة لان عدتها قرؤان وطلاقها ثنتان ترجمہ اور یہی حکم مکاتبہ (باندی) کا ہے۔ یعنی جب اپنے مولی کی اجازت سے نکاح کیا پھر وہ آزاد ہوگئی اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ اس کیلئے خیار نہیں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ عقد اس پر اس کی رضامندی سے نافذ کیا گیا ہے۔ اور مہر بھی مکاتبہ کیلئے ہے۔ لہذا اثبات خیار کے کوئی معنی نہیں ہیں۔ بخلاف باندی کے کیونکہ اسکی رضامندی معتبر نہیں ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ علت خیار از دیار ملک ہے۔ ہم نے اس کو مکاتبہ میں بھی پایا۔ اس لئے کہ مکاتبہ کی عدت دو حیض اور اس کی طلاق دو ہیں۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مکاتبہ نے اپنے مولی کی اجازت سے نکاح کیا۔ پھر مکاتبہ بدل کتابت ادا کر کے آزاد ہوگئی تو ائمہ ثلث کے نزدیک اس کیلئے خیار معتق حاصل نہیں ہوگا۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ باندی معتقہ کیلئے ثبوت خیار دوجہوں سے تھا۔ ایک یہ کہ باندی کا عقد نکاح بغیر اس کی رضا مندی کے نافلہ تھا دوم یہ کہ اس کا مہر اس کے مولیٰ کے لیے تھا اور مکاتبہ میں یہ دونوں باتیں موجود نہیں ہیں کیونکہ مکاتبہ کا عقد نکاح بغیر اس کی رضا مندی کے نافذ نہیں تھا اور مہر بھی اسی کیلئے ہو گا نہ کہ اس کے مولیٰ کے لئے لہذا مکاتبہ کے لئے آزاد ہونے کے بعد خیار محتق ثابت نہیں ہوگا لیکن اگر کوئی اعتراض کرے کہ اگر مملوکہ باندی کی رضامندی سے نکاح ہوا ہو تو اس کے لیے بھی خیار عتق ثابت نہ ہونا چاہئے تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مملوکہ باندی کی رضامندی کا اعتبار نہیں کیا گیا ہے ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ آزادی کے بعد خیار عتق کی علت معتقہ باندی پر ملک طلاق کا بڑھ جاتا ہے۔ اور یہ علت مکاتبہ میں موجود ہے۔ کیونکہ مکاتبہ کی عدت آزاد ہونے سے پہلے دو حیض تھے اور آزاد ہونے کے بعد تین حیض ہو جائیں گے۔ اسی طرح آزاد ہونے سے پہلے اس کا شوہر دو طلاقوں کا مالک تھا آزاد ہونے سے تین طلاقوں کا مالک ہوگا۔ پس جب خیار محقق کی علت مکاتبہ میں موجود ہے تو مکاتبہ کے آزاد ہونے کے بعد اس کیلئے بھی خیار معتق حاصل ہوگا۔
A mukatabah married with her husband's permission, then was freed; she also has the option. Similarly, the mukatabah: meaning when she marries with her master's permission, then is freed. Zufar said she has no option because the contract was executed with her consent and the dower is for her, so there is no point in establishing the option, unlike the slave woman because her consent is not considered. Our proof is that the cause is the increase in ownership, and we find it in the mukatabah because her iddah is two menstrual cycles and her divorce is two. Translation: And this same ruling applies to the mukatabah (slave woman). I.e., when she married with her master's permission, then she was freed. Imam Zufar said she has no option because the contract was executed with her consent and the dower is for her, so there is no meaning to establishing the option, unlike the slave woman because her consent is not considered. Our proof is that the cause of the option is the increase in ownership; we have found it in the mukatabah as well, because the mukatabah's iddah is two menstrual cycles and her divorce is two. Explanation: The case is that if a mukatabah married with her master's permission, then she paid the kitabah and became free, according to the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) she does have the option. Imam Zufar's proof is that for a freed slave woman, the option is established from two aspects: first, her contract was executed without her consent; second, her dower was for her master. In the case of a mukatabah, both these are absent because her contract was not executed without her consent, and the dower is for herself, not for her master. So she should not have the option after freedom. But if one objects that if a regular slave woman married with her consent, she too should not have the option, the answer is that a regular slave woman's consent is not considered. Our proof is that the cause of the option after emancipation is the increase in the number of divorces she owns. This cause exists in the mukatabah, because her iddah before freedom was two cycles, after freedom becomes three; similarly, before freedom her husband owned two divorces, after freedom he owns three. So when the cause of the option exists in the mukatabah, she also obtains the option after freedom.
Source pages p. 164

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Zufar and the majority Hanafi imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) regarding whether a mukatabah (a slave woman with a contract of manumission) who marries with her master's permission and then becomes free has the option (khiyar al-itiq) to annul her marriage. Zufar argues that she should not have the option because, unlike a regular slave woman, her marriage was with her consent and the dower belongs to her, not her master. Therefore, the grounds for the option do not apply. However, the majority Hanafis argue that the underlying cause ('illa) of the option is the increase in ownership that occurs upon freedom: the husband gains additional divorces and the woman's iddah lengthens. Since this cause also exists for a freed mukatabah, she too should have the option. The text emphasizes that the consent of a regular slave woman is not considered legitimate, so the comparison fails. This highlights the Hanafi method of focusing on the effective cause ('illa) rather than apparent similarities or differences.

Key Terms
مکاتبہ (mukatabah): A female slave who has made a contract (kitabah) with her master to purchase her freedom by paying installments.
ازدیاد ملک (izdiyad al-milk): Increase in ownership: the change in rights over divorce and iddah duration upon freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view, why does a freed mukatabah have khiyar al-itiq?
A) Because she married without her master's permission.
B) Because her husband was a slave at the time of marriage.
C) Because the cause of the option—increase in ownership—exists for her as well.
D) Because Imam Zufar's opinion is preferred.

Key Takeaway
The increase in ownership upon freedom is the effective cause for khiyar al-itiq, applying equally to freed mukatabahs and regular slave women, irrespective of consent.

Marriage of a Slave Woman Without Master's Permission: Ruling Upon Freedom
Ruling on an amah who married without permission and was later freed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the validity of a slave woman's marriage contracted without her master's permission when she is later freed, and explain why she does not acquire the option (khiyar) upon freedom.

Core Idea
A suspended marriage becomes effective upon freedom; no khiyar arises because the marriage was not effective before freedom.

We have seen that when a slave woman marries with her master's permission and is then freed, she gains the option of puberty (khiyar al-itiq). But what if she married without permission? This lesson examines a distinct ruling: the marriage becomes valid upon freedom, but she gains no option. Understanding why requires distinguishing between the capacity to contract (ahliyyat al-ibarah) and the effectiveness of the contract (nufudh).

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal status of the marriage before freedom
A marriage contracted without the master's permission is sound in itself (sahih) but not effective (nāfidh). It is suspended (mawqūf) on the master's consent.
2
Determine what happens upon the master's freedom
When the master frees the slave, the master's right (which was blocking effectiveness) ceases. The marriage becomes fully effective (nāfidh) automatically, without needing fresh consent.
3
Analyze the absence of khiyar al-itiq
The khiyar arises only when there is an increase in ownership (ziyādat al-milk). Here, the marriage only becomes effective after freedom, so there was no effective marriage before freedom. Hence, no increase occurs.
4
Contrast with the case of marriage with permission
If she had married with permission, the marriage was effective from the start, and freedom then brings an increase (she becomes her own guardian), triggering the option. Without permission, no such increase.
5
Apply the principle of ahliyyat al-ibarah
The slave woman has the capacity to contract (ahliyyat al-ibarah) even without permission; the obstacle is external (master's right). The contract is valid but not effectual.
See key terms for definitions.

And if a slave woman married without her master's permission, then she was freed, the marriage is valid (effective) because she has the capacity of expression, and the lack of effect was due to the master's right, and it has ceased. And she has no option because the effect occurred after freedom, so an increase in ownership does not materialize, just as if she married herself after freedom. Translation: And if a slave woman married without her master's permission, then she was freed, the marriage becomes valid (effective) because she has the capacity of expression, and the prevention of effect was due to the master's right, and that has ceased. And the slave woman has no option, because effectiveness occurred after freedom, so an increase in ownership is not realized, just as if she married herself after freedom. Explanation: There are two points: first, if a slave woman married without her master's permission and then was freed, this marriage becomes valid (effective). Second, this freed slave woman does not have the option (khiyar al-itiq). The proof of validity is that the requirements of marriage are present because the pillar is there.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage states a ruling: a slave woman who marries without her master's permission enters a contract that is suspended (mawquf) on her master's consent. If the master later frees her, the marriage becomes immediately valid (nafidh) because the only impediment (the master's right) is removed. The woman does not gain khiyar al-itiq because the marriage only becomes fully effective after freedom, so the 'increase in ownership' that triggers the option never occurs—she was not in a fully effective marriage before freedom. The ruling is contrasted with the previous cases where the marriage was effective from the start (with master's permission) and then freedom brings an increase. This lesson clarifies that the option is tied to a change in status within an already valid marriage, not to the new validation of a suspended one.

Key Terms
اهلیة العبارة (ahliyyat al-'ibarah): Capacity to execute a contract: the woman has the legal ability to express her consent, but was prevented by her master's right.
نفوذ (nufudh): Effectiveness: the contract becomes fully operative and binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A slave woman's marriage without permission becomes valid upon freedom, with no right of annulment because the marriage was not effective before freedom.

Khiyar al-'Itq for a Mukatabah: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on khiyar al-'itq for a mukatabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school grants the khiyar al-'itq to a mukatabah and how the cause ('illa) of increased ownership differentiates her from a regular slave woman.

Core Idea
The option of emancipation is based on increase in husband's right to divorce, not consent or dower.

This passage from al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the khiyar al-'itq (option of emancipation) for a mukatabah. While Imam Zufar argues that consent and dower negate the option, the majority of the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) rely on the increase in the husband's ownership of divorce as the cause. Understanding this dispute reveals how causal reasoning (talil) operates in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The issue is whether a mukatabah who marries with her master's permission and later becomes free has the right to repudiate her marriage (khiyar al-'itq).
The mukatabah is a slave woman under a kitabah contract.
2
State the majority Hanafi position and its proof
The three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) hold that she has the option. Their proof is that the cause ('illa) is the increase in the husband's ownership of divorce, which occurs because her 'iddah and number of divorces increase upon emancipation.
Before emancipation: 'iddah = 2 menstrual periods, husband has 2 divorces. After: 'iddah = 3, husband has 3.
3
State Imam Zufar's opposing view and his proof
Imam Zufar denies the option. He argues that the marriage was validly contracted with her consent and the dower is for her, so there is no increase in the husband's ownership over her.
He analogizes to a free woman who consents, who has no such option.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
The Hanafi response is that the cause is not consent or dower but the increase in the husband's right to divorce, which is present for the mukatabah. This differentiates her from a regular slave woman, whose consent is irrelevant.
For an ordinary slave woman, the husband's ownership does not increase upon emancipation because her 'iddah and divorces remain the same? Actually, an ordinary slave woman's 'iddah is also two, but the cause is not present because she is not under kitabah? The passage focuses on mukatabah.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf and mufta bihi
The practical consequence: if the husband divorces the mukatabah once before emancipation, he has one remaining divorce; after emancipation, he has two remaining if she stays married. The option allows her to end the marriage and reset the divorce count. The relied-upon position is that of the three imams, granting the option.
If she exercises the option, the marriage ends without divorce, preserving the husband's divorce count.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نفذ عليها برضاها و كان المهر لها فلا معنى لاثبات الخيار بخلاف الامة لانه لا يعتبر رضاها ولنا ان العلة ازدياد الملک وقد وجدناها فى المكاتبة لان عدتها قرؤان وطلاقها ثنتان
It is executed with her consent, and the dower is for her, so there is no meaning to establishing the option, unlike the slave woman because her consent is not considered. And our evidence is that the cause is the increase in ownership, and we have found it in the mukatabah because her waiting period is two menstrual periods and her divorce is two.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the khiyar al-'itq (option of emancipation) for a mukatabah (a slave woman who has a contract of kitabah). The ruling states that if a mukatabah marries with her master's permission and then becomes free, she does not have the option to repudiate the marriage (khiyar al-'itq). Imam Zufar disagrees and argues that the option is not established because the marriage was validly contracted with her consent and the dower is for her, unlike an ordinary slave woman whose consent is not considered. The Hanafi position (Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) responds that the cause ('illa) for the option is the increase in the husband's ownership of divorce (i.e., the increase in his right to divorce). This cause is found in the mukatabah because before emancipation, her waiting period is two menstrual periods and her husband has only two divorces; after emancipation, her waiting period becomes three and the husband gains three divorces. Therefore, the increase in ownership occurs, so the option is established. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of the three imams, granting the option to the mukatabah.

Key Terms
مكاتبة (mukatabah): A slave woman who has entered into a contract of kitabah with her master, agreeing to pay a sum for her freedom.
خيار عتق (khiyar al-'itq): The option of emancipation; the right of a slave woman upon becoming free to repudiate or continue her marriage.
علة ('illa): The effective cause in legal reasoning; here, the increase in the husband's ownership of divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because her consent was not considered.
B) Because her dower was for her master.
C) Because the husband's right to divorce increases upon her emancipation.
D) Because she is now free and can choose anything.

Key Takeaway
The khiyar al-'itq for a mukatabah is established because the cause is the increase in the husband's right to divorce, not the consent of the slave woman.

Khiyar al-'Itq for a Slave Woman Marrying Without Permission
Ruling that such a slave has no khiyar al-'itq after emancipation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on khiyar al-'itq for a slave woman who married without permission and explain the qiyas basis for denying the option.

Core Idea
No khiyar al-'itq because the marriage only becomes effective after emancipation — no increase in ownership.

This passage addresses a specific scenario in nikah: a slave woman marries without her master's permission, then is freed. Does she have the option to repudiate the marriage (khiyar al-'itq)? The Hanafi school rules that the marriage becomes valid upon emancipation, but she has no such option. We will examine the reasoning behind this, which rests on the concept of ownership of divorce and a qiyas to a free woman.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a slave woman marrying without her master's permission, then being freed. The ruling is: the marriage becomes valid (sahih) upon emancipation, and she has no khiyar al-'itq (option to repudiate).
2
Locate the dalil
The author provides a qiyas (analogical reasoning) to support the denial of the option. The analogy is to a free woman who marries herself — in that case, there is no khiyar al-'itq because there is no increase in the husband's ownership of divorce.
The qiyas is over the effective cause (illa): absence of any increase in ownership.
3
Analyze the illa (effective cause)
The khiyar al-'itq is only granted when the marriage contract was valid and effective at the time of contract, and later emancipation increases the husband's rights (e.g., he gains more control over divorce or inheritance). Here, the marriage was not effective at contract time due to the master's right; it only became effective after freedom. Hence, emancipation does not increase ownership — it merely activates a suspended contract.
The illa is 'no increase in ownership' — a khafiyyah (subtle) cause.
4
Understand the basis: suspension, not void
The marriage is not batil (void) but mawquf (suspended). The slave woman is ahl al-'ibarah (legally competent), so the contract is valid in itself. The master's right only prevented enforcement (nafidh). Once the master's right ceases (by emancipation), the contract becomes enforceable without any new consent.
This distinguishes it from a completely invalid contract where no emancipation can cure it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان تزوجت امة بغير اذن مولاهاثم عتقت صح النكاح لانها من اهل العبارة وامتناع النفوذ لحق المولى وقدزال ولاخيار لها لان النفوذ بعد العتق فلا تتحقق زيادة الملك كما اذا زوجت نفسها بعد العتق
And if a slave woman marries without her master's permission, then she is emancipated, the marriage is valid because she is among those capable of expression, and the prevention of effect was due to the right of the master, and it has ceased. And she has no option because the effect occurred after emancipation, so no increase in ownership is realized, just as if she married herself after emancipation.
Source pages p. 165

Commentary
This passage states two rulings: (1) If a slave woman marries without her master's permission and is later freed, the marriage becomes valid (nafidh) upon emancipation. This is because the slave woman is legally competent (ahl al-'ibarah), and the only impediment was the master's right, which ceased upon emancipation. (2) She does not have the khiyar al-'itq (option to repudiate the marriage) because the marriage only became effective after emancipation. The cause for the option is the increase in the husband's ownership of divorce, but here the ownership did not increase because the marriage was already in effect only after freedom. This is analogous to her marrying herself after being freed, in which case no option exists.

Key Terms
أهل العبارة (ahl al-'ibarah): Those capable of expression and legal competence; a legally competent person.
نفوذ (nafidh): Effectiveness or execution of a contract; here it means the marriage becomes legally binding.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Because she was not legally competent.

C) Because the marriage only became effective after emancipation, so no increase in ownership.
D) Because she was forced.

Key Takeaway
A slave woman who marries without permission and is later freed gains a valid marriage but no khiyar al-'itq, because the option requires an increase in ownership that did not occur here.

The Mahr of a Slave Woman: Who Receives It and Why?
Ruling on who receives the mahr depending on consummation timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that the mahr in a suspended marriage belongs to the owner of the slave's benefits at the time of consummation.

Core Idea
The mahr goes to the owner of the benefits at consummation, not the one who specified it.

This passage examines a key rule in Hanafi marriage law: when a slave woman marries without her master's permission, the marriage is suspended. Upon emancipation, the contract becomes retroactively valid. The critical question addressed here is who receives the specified mahr—the master or the freedwoman—and the answer hinges entirely on when consummation occurred relative to emancipation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a suspended marriage (nikah mawquf) of a slave woman who marries without her master's permission, specifying a mahr higher than her mahr al-mithl. The ruling is that the specified mahr is due, but its recipient depends on the timing of consummation relative to emancipation.
The marriage is initially suspended because of the lack of permission; it becomes effective upon emancipation.
2
Understand the principle of retroactive effectiveness (isti'naad)
Upon emancipation, the contract becomes effective retroactively to the time it was entered into. This validates the specified mahr and makes it obligatory, even though the contract was initially suspended.
This principle is unique to Hanafi fiqh and explains why the mahr is not replaced with mahr al-mithl.
3
Determine who owned the benefits at the time of consummation
The mahr is compensation for the husband deriving benefit from the slave woman. If consummation occurred before emancipation, the benefits belonged to the master, so the mahr goes to the master. If after emancipation, the benefits belonged to the freedwoman, so the mahr goes to her.
This is the key analytical step: the timing of consummation decides the recipient.
4
Apply the reasoning to confirm no additional mahr is due
Because the contract is single and becomes effective retroactively, it imposes only one dower. Even if intercourse occurred within the suspended marriage, no additional mahr is due beyond the specified one.
This reinforces the principle that the contract is unified.
5
Note the practical outcome
The slave woman receives the full specified mahr (e.g., 1000) if consummation occurred after emancipation, even if her mahr al-mithl is lower. This shows the importance of retroactive validity.
The specified mahr is binding, not the mahr al-mithl.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان كانت تزوجت بغیر اذنه على الف ومهر مثلها مائة فدخل بها زوجها ثم اعتقها مولاها فالمهر للمولى لانه استوفى منافع مملوكة للمولى وان لم يدخل بهاحتى اعتقها فالمهر لهالانه استوفى منافع مملوكة لها والمراد بالمهر الالف المسمى لان نفاذ العقد بالعتق استندالى وقت وجود العقد فصحت التسمية ووجب المسمى ولهذا لم يجب مهر اخر بالوطي فى نكاح موقوف لان العقد قد تحد باستناد النفاذ فلايوجب الامهر او احدا
For if she married without his permission for one thousand while her mahr al-mithl is one hundred, and her husband consummated with her, then her master emancipated her, then the dower is for the master because he [the husband] received benefits owned by the master. And if he did not consummate with her until he emancipated her, then the dower is for her because he received benefits owned by her. And the intended meaning by 'dower' is the specified one thousand because the effectiveness of the contract by emancipation is attributed back to the time of the contract's existence, so the specification is valid and the specified amount is obligatory. And for this reason, no other dower is obligatory by intercourse in a suspended marriage because the contract is single due to the attribution of effectiveness, so it only imposes one dower.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This passage addresses the mahr (dower) in a case where a slave woman marries without her master's permission, specifying a mahr that exceeds her mahr al-mithl. Two scenarios are distinguished: (1) If the husband consummates the marriage before the slave is emancipated, the full specified mahr goes to the master. The reason is that the husband derived benefit from the slave's services, which belonged to the master at that time. The master is entitled to compensation. (2) If the husband does not consummate until after emancipation, the mahr goes to the freed woman herself. Because the benefit was received after she owned herself. The specified mahr (one thousand) is obligatory because upon emancipation the marriage contract becomes effective retroactively to the time of the contract, so the specified dower is valid and owed. No additional dower is due for the intercourse that occurred in the suspended marriage because there is only one contract, and it imposes only one dower.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The dower of a woman similar to the bride in status; used as a benchmark.
نكاح موقوف (nikah mawquf): A suspended marriage: a marriage that is not effective immediately due to an impediment that may be removed (e.g., master's permission).
استناد (isti'naad): Attribution or ascription: here, the effectiveness of the contract is attributed back to the time of the contract's inception.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The husband.
B) The slave woman.
C) The master.

Key Takeaway
The recipient of the mahr in a suspended marriage is determined by the time of consummation, not the time of the contract or specification.

Dower of a Slave Girl: Retroactive Validity and Usufruct
Ruling-on dower entitlement with retroactive validity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of retroactive validity (istinad al-nafadh) to determine who receives the dower when a slave girl marries without permission and is subsequently freed.

Core Idea
The dower compensates the owner of the usufruct at consummation; the contract's validity is retroactive.

In this lesson, we examine a nuanced case from al-Hidayah: a slave girl marries without her master's permission, naming a dower far exceeding her proper dower. The marriage is suspended (mawquf) pending the master's approval. If the husband consummates, the dower goes to the master or the slave girl depending on whether freedom occurs before or after consummation. The key is that the dower compensates the one who owned the usufruct (manafi') at the time of intercourse. Additionally, because the contract becomes valid retroactively upon manumission, the named dower is upheld even if it exceeds the proper dower. This ruling illustrates the Hanafi principles of istinad al-nafadh and the treatment of manafi' as compensable property.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Scenario
A slave girl marries without her master's permission, naming a specific dower (mahr al-musamma) that is higher than her proper dower (mahr al-mithl). The husband consummates either before or after the master frees her. Identify the two possible timelines.
The marriage is suspended (mawquf) until the master's approval, but emancipation acts as implicit approval.
2
Identify the Legal Basis: Compensation for Usufruct
The dower is understood as compensation for the usufruct (manafi') of the wife's body. The usufruct belongs to the master as long as she is a slave; upon freedom, it belongs to her. Therefore, the dower follows the owner of the usufruct at the time of consummation.
This is the underlying ʻillah (effective cause) for the ruling.
3
Apply the Rule to Both Timelines
If consummation occurs before manumission, the usufruct belonged to the master, so the dower goes to the master. If consummation occurs after manumission, the usufruct belonged to the slave girl, so the dower goes to her. The entire named dower is due, not adjusted to mahr al-mithl.
No splitting of dower.
4
Recognize Retroactive Validity (Istinad al-Nafadh)
The master's emancipation makes the marriage valid retroactively to the time of the contract. This means the named dower is binding as if the contract were valid from the start. Therefore, the named amount (mahr al-musamma) is owed, not the proper dower (mahr al-mithl).
This principle is unique to the Hanafi school; other schools may treat the marriage as a new contract after approval.
5
Consider Cross-Madhhab Implications
The Shafi'i school objects that the slave girl could not legally consent to a dower exceeding her mahr al-mithl, thus the excess is invalid. The Hanafi response relies on retroactive validity: since the contract is now valid from inception, the naming stands. Understand this ikhtilaf and its practical consequence.
This step strengthens your ability to compare schools.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فان كانت تزوجت بغیر اذنه على الف ومهر مثلها مائة فدخل بها زوجها ثم اعتقها مولاها فالمهر للمولى لانه استوفى منافع مملوكة للمولى وان لم يدخل بهاحتى اعتقها فالمهر لهالانه استوفى منافع مملوكة لها والمراد بالمهر الالف المسمى لان نفاذ العقد بالعتق استندالى وقت وجود العقد فصحت التسمية ووجب المسمى ولهذا لم يجب مهر اخر بالوطي فى نكاح موقوف لان العقد قد تحد باستناد النفاذ فلايوجب الامهر او احدا
So if she married without his permission for a thousand (dirhams) while her proper dower is a hundred, and her husband consummated with her, then her master freed her, then the dower is for the master because he (the husband) received usufruct belonging to the master. And if he did not consummate with her until he freed her, then the dower is for her because he received usufruct belonging to her. And what is meant by the dower is the named thousand, because the validity of the contract by emancipation is retroactive to the time of the contract's existence, so the naming is valid and the named amount becomes obligatory. For this reason, no other dower is due by intercourse in a suspended marriage, because the contract is unified due to the retroactive force and thus only one dower is due.
Source pages p. 166

Commentary
This is a ruling-with-proof passage from the commentary on al-Hidayah. The issue: a slave girl marries without her master's permission, naming a dower of 1000 dirhams, while her proper dower (mahr al-mithl) is only 100. The husband consummates, then the master frees her. The ruling: if consummation occurs before manumission, the entire named dower goes to the master. The reason is that the husband derived the usufruct (manafi') of the slave girl's body, which at that time belonged to the master. If instead the manumission occurred before consummation, then the dower goes to the slave girl because the usufruct belonged to her after freedom. The author clarifies that the dower claimed is the named one (1000), not the proper dower, because the validity of the marriage (nafadh) is retroactively assigned to the time of the contract due to the master's subsequent freeing/approval. Therefore the naming of the dower is upheld. This also explains why in a suspended marriage (nikah mawquf), if intercourse occurs both before and after approval, only one dower is due: the contract is one and the retroactivity makes it as if the contract was valid from the start.

Key Terms
مهر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The proper dower: the amount of dower appropriate for a woman of similar status, determined by factors like family, beauty, etc.
مهر مسمى (mahr al-musamma): The named dower: the specific amount agreed upon in the marriage contract.
استناد النفاذ (istinad al-nafadh): Retroactive validity: the legal effect of the contract (nafadh) is assigned back to the time of the contract when a subsequent cause (like emancipation/approval) completes its conditions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A slave girl marries without her master's permission, naming a dower of 1000 dirhams (mahr al-mithl 100). The husband consummates before the master frees her. According to the Hanafi ruling in the passage, who receives the dower and how much?
A) The master receives 100 dirhams (mahr al-mithl).
B) The master receives 1000 dirhams.
C) The slave girl receives 1000 dirhams.
D) The slave girl receives 100 dirhams.

Key Takeaway
The dower is compensation for usufruct at the time of consummation; retroactive validity ensures the named dower is binding even if it exceeds the proper dower.

The Father and the Son's Slave Girl: No Mahr Due
Ruling on father's liability for son's slave girl he impregnates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a father's intercourse with his son's slave girl and identify the thamarah al-khilaf between the Hanafi school and Zufar/Shafi'i.

Core Idea
A father's wilaya over his son's property transforms intercourse with the son's slave girl into intercourse with his own property, eliminating the obligation of mahr.

This passage presents a nuanced Hanafi ruling that integrates property guardianship (wilaya), sexual needs, and the acquisition of umm walad status. The father's intercourse with his son's slave girl, resulting in a child, triggers multiple legal consequences: the slave girl becomes an umm walad for the father, he must compensate his son for the slave's value, but no mahr is due. The reasoning hinges on the father's authority to own the slave girl for his necessity before the birth, making the intercourse occur within his own property. A key disagreement with Zufar (within the Hanafi school) and al-Shafi'i centers on whether mahr is required. Understanding this ruling deepens your grasp of how necessity-based ownership interacts with slavery and family law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal scenario
The scenario: a father (the son's father) has intercourse with his son's slave girl, she gives birth, and the father claims the child. Determine the legal status of the slave girl and the father's obligations.
The father must claim the child for umm walad status to apply.
2
State the Hanafi ruling and its components
The Hanafi ruling: (1) the slave girl becomes the father's umm walad, (2) the father must pay the slave's value to his son, (3) no mahr is due. Understand each component's basis.
Umm walad status frees her upon the father's death.
3
Analyze the reasoning (ta'lil) for no mahr
The father has wilaya over his son's property for necessity (such as preserving his life and controlling desire). He can own the slave girl by paying her value, and this ownership is established before birth as a condition for umm walad. Therefore, intercourse meets his own property, so no mahr.
The need for controlling desire is considered a necessity like food, but for a slave girl, he must pay value.
4
Identify the opposing position and its proof
Zufar (Hanafi) and al-Shafi'i argue that mahr is due because ownership is only established by the birth (istilad), which is after intercourse. At the time of intercourse, the slave girl belonged to the son. They analogize to a jointly-owned slave girl where mahr is shared.
The key difference: timing of ownership establishment.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: under the Hanafi position, the father pays only the value of the slave girl to the son. Under the opposing view, he would also pay mahr to the slave girl (or her owner, but here the son becomes owner after birth?). Thus, a financial difference.
The Hanafi position avoids double payment.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و من وطى امة ابنه فولدت منه فهى ام ولدله وعليه قيمتها ولا مهر عليه ومعنى المسألة ان يدعيه الاب ووجهه ان له ولاية تملک مالا ابنه للحاجة الى البقاء فله تملك جاريته للحاجة الى صيانة الماء غيران الحاجة الى ابقاء نسله دونها الى ابقاء نفسه فلهذا يتملك الجارية بالقيمة والطعام بغير القيمة ثم هذا الملك يثبت قبل الاستيلاد شَرْطَالُه اذالمصحح حقيقة الملك او حقه وكل ذلك غير ثابت للاب فيها حتى يجوز له التزوج بها فلابد من تقديمه فتبين ان الوطي يلاقي ملكه فلايلزمه العقر وقال زفر والشافعي رحمهما الله يجب المهر لانهما يثبتان الملك حكما للاستيلاد كما فى الجارية المشتركة وحكم الشئى يعقبه والمسألة معروفة
And whoever has intercourse with his son's slave girl and she gives birth from him, then she is an umm walad for him, and he must pay her value (to the son), and there is no mahr upon him. The meaning of the case is that the father claims the child. The reasoning is that he has guardianship (wilaya) over his son's property for the need of preserving his own life; so he has the right to own his son's slave girl for the need of preserving his (sexual) desire. However, the need to preserve his offspring is less than the need to preserve his own self. For this reason, he becomes owner of the slave girl by (paying) her value, while food (necessary for survival) is taken without value. Then this ownership is established before the birth of the child as a condition for him (to be considered owner) because it validates the reality of ownership or its right. And all that is not established for the father with respect to her so that he may marry her; it is necessary to precede (ownership). So it becomes clear that the intercourse meets his ownership, so no dower is due. And Zufar and al-Shafi'i (may Allah have mercy on them) said: The mahr is obligatory because they establish ownership by legal consequence of istilad (giving birth to a child after intercourse) just as in the case of a jointly-owned slave girl, and the ruling of a thing follows it. And this case is well-known.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the Hanafi school and includes a dispute with Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) and al-Shafi'i. The case: a man has intercourse with his son's slave girl, she gives birth to a child whom the father claims. The Hanafi ruling: the slave girl becomes an umm walad (mother of the master's child) for the father, meaning she is free upon his death and the child is free. The father must pay the value of the slave girl to his son (compensation for the property), but no mahr (dower) is due. The reasoning: the father has a legal guardianship (wilaya) over his son's property for his own necessity (al-haja ila al-baqa' — the need for survival). This includes the need to control his sexual desire, which is considered a necessity. However, this guardianship is limited; it allows him to take food without compensation in dire need, but for a slave girl, he must pay the value. Ownership (milk) is established before the birth of the child as a condition (shart) for her to become umm walad. This ownership makes the intercourse legally occurring within his own property, so no mahr is due (as intercourse with one's own slave does not require mahr). Zufar and al-Shafi'i argue that mahr is obligatory because ownership is established only by the birth itself (istilad), not before; thus at the time of intercourse, the slave girl was still the son's property, so mahr is due. The Hanafi response is implicit: that ownership is established before birth by the father's right to take the slave girl for his need, so intercourse meets his ownership.

Key Terms
ام ولد (umm walad): A slave girl who gives birth to a child by her master; upon the master's death, she becomes free.
ولایت (wilaya): Legal authority or guardianship; here, the father's authority over his son's property for the son's benefit but also for the father's necessity under dire need.
عقر (aqr): Dower (mahr) in the context of intercourse with a woman; often used for the compensation due for sexual intercourse that is not within a valid marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A father has intercourse with his son's slave girl, she gives birth, and the father claims the child. According to the Hanafi school, what are the father's obligations?
A) He must pay the value of the slave girl to his son and also pay mahr to the slave girl.
B) He must pay only the value of the slave girl to his son; no mahr is due.
C) He must pay only mahr to the slave girl; no compensation to his son.
D) He has no obligations because the child makes her umm walad.

Key Takeaway
The father's wilaya for necessity allows him to own his son's slave girl before birth, making intercourse with her legally equivalent to intercourse with his own property, thus no mahr is due; only the value of the slave girl is payable to the son.

The Mahr When a Slave Girl Is Freed After Marriage
Objection and response regarding mahr of a freed slave girl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on mahr when a slave girl is freed after marriage, explain the principle of retroactive enforcement (nafadh), and apply the distinction based on the timing of freedom (before or after dukhul).

Core Idea
The specified mahr is due, not mahr al-mithl, because enforcement is retroactive to the contract.

This passage from al-Hidayah resolves a subtle objection regarding the mahr of a slave girl who marries with her master's permission and is later freed. An objector argues that the master should only receive mahr al-mithl (the fair dower for a slave), not the specified amount. The Hanafi reply, grounded in the principle of nafadh (retroactive enforcement), affirms that the specified mahr stands. Understanding this ruling clarifies how Hanafi law treats suspended contracts and the attribution of legal effects to the time of agreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
Read the opening of the passage and isolate the objector's claim. The objector argues that if intercourse occurs before the slave girl is freed, the master should receive only mahr al-mithl (the fair value of a slave's vulva) and any excess should go to the woman, because the vulva belonged to the master at that time.
The objection is based on the idea that the master's property right in the vulva should limit his entitlement to its objective value.
2
Understand the Hanafi Response
Al-Hidayah responds that the mahr referred to is the specified mahr (musamma) agreed upon at the time of the contract, not mahr al-mithl. The reason is that the enforcement (nafadh) of the contract is retroactively attributed to the time the contract was made. Since the contract was for a specified one thousand, that specification becomes valid upon enforcement.
The key legal maxim: nafadh is attributed to the time of the contract (wujud al-'aqd).
3
Distinguish Based on Timing of Freedom
The ruling then differentiates: if she is freed after dukhul (intercourse), the mahr goes to the master (because the vulva was his property at the time of intercourse). If she is freed before dukhul, the mahr goes to the woman herself (since she becomes the owner of her vulva upon freedom and the mahr compensates her).
This distinction flows from the principle that the mahr is a compensation for the vulva (budd').
4
Analyze the Analogy of Nikah Mawquf
The passage brings an analogy: a slave girl who marries without the master's permission (a suspended contract) and later gains permission. In that case, only one mahr is due because the permission retroactively validates all acts of intercourse from the beginning, making the entire marriage valid from inception. This parallels the case of freedom.
The analogy reinforces that enforcement retroactively unifies the contract, preventing multiple mahr obligations.
5
Extract the Principle of Nafadh
The core principle is that when a suspended contract is enforced (by permission or subsequent capacity), the enforcement is backdated to the time of the contract. Hence, all terms (including mahr specification) are valid from the start, and any acts performed during the suspension are treated as part of a single valid marriage.
This principle is applied in other areas of Hanafi law, such as in sales and agency.

والمراد بالمهر الاف المسمى سے ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے۔ اعتراض یہ ہے کہ دخول قبل العتق کی صورت میں مولیٰ کیلئے مہر مثل کی مقدار واجب ہونا چاہئے اور جو مہر مثل سے زائد ہو وہ عورت کو دے دیا جائے۔ کیونکہ من کل وجہ بضع کی قیمت مہر مثل ہے۔ اور بضع مولی کی ملک ہے لہذا بضع کی قیمت مولی کیلئے ہونی چاہئے نہ کہ قیمت سے زائد۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے جواب میں فرمایا کہ مہر سے مراد ایک ہزار سمی ہے نہ کہ مہر مثل ۔ اسلئے کہ باندی کے آزاد ہونے کی وجہ سے عقد کا نفاذ وجود عقد کے وقت کی طرف منسوب ہوگا۔ یعنی جس وقت نکاح منعقد ہوا تھا اسی وقت سے نفاذ ہو گا۔ اگر چہ نفاذ کا اظہار آزادی کے بعد ہوا اور نکاح منعقد ہوا تھا ایک ہزار سمی پر پس یہ تسمیہ صحیح ہو گیا۔ اور سمی واجب ہو گا صرف یہ کلام ہے کہ اگر دخول کے بعد آزاد کی گئی تو یہ مہر مولی کا ہوگا۔ اور اگر دخول سے پہلے آزاد ہوئی تو یہ مہر اسی باندی کا ہوگا۔ اور اسی وجہ سے نفاذ عقد وجود عقد کی طرف منسوب ہے۔ نکاح موقوف میں وطی کی وجہ سے دوسرا مہر واجب نہیں ہو گا۔ مثلا باندی نے بغیر مولی کی اجازت کے نکاح کیا۔ پھر مولیٰ نے اجازت دے دی تو یہ نہیں ہو گا کہ اجازت سے پہلے جو وطی کی گئی ہے اس کا مہر واجب ہو۔ پھر اجازت کے بعد وطی سے مہر سمی واجب ہو ۔ کیونکہ اجازت سے جب وہی عقد نافذ ہوا جو موقوف تھا تو گویا عقد کے وقت ہی اجازت ہو چکی تو ہر ایک وطی نکاح جائز میں واقع ہوئی۔ لہذا ایک ہی مہر لازم ہو گا۔ یعنی نفاذ وقت عقد کی طرف منسوب ہونے سے ایک ہی عقد رہا۔ دو عقد نہیں اور ایک عقد سے ایک مہر واجب ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا یہاں بھی ایک ہی مہر واجب ہوگا۔
And the meaning of mahr is a response to an objection regarding the specified one thousand. The objection is that in the case of intercourse before emancipation, the master should owe the amount of mahr al-mithl, and whatever exceeds mahr al-mithl should be given to the woman. Because in every respect, the value of the vulva is mahr al-mithl. And the vulva belongs to the master, so its value should be for the master, not more than the value. The author of al-Hidayah responded that by mahr is meant the specified one thousand, not mahr al-mithl. This is because due to the emancipation of the slave girl, the enforcement of the contract is attributed to the time of the contract. That is, from the time the marriage was contracted, enforcement takes place, even though the manifestation of enforcement occurs after emancipation. And the marriage was contracted on a specified one thousand, so this specification became valid, and the specified mahr is wajib. Only this is said: if she was emancipated after intercourse, then this mahr belongs to the master; if she was emancipated before intercourse, then this mahr belongs to the slave girl herself. And for this reason, the enforcement of the contract is attributed to the existence of the contract. In a suspended marriage, a second mahr is not due due to intercourse. For example, a slave girl married without the master's permission, then the master gave permission: it will not be that a mahr is due for the intercourse that occurred before permission, and then a specified mahr is due for intercourse after permission. Because when the same suspended contract is enforced by permission, it is as if permission occurred at the time of the contract, so every intercourse occurred in a valid marriage. Hence, only one mahr becomes binding. That is, due to enforcement being attributed to the time of the contract, it remains one contract, not two, and from one contract one mahr is wajib. So here too, only one mahr is wajib.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is an expansion from al-Hidayah addressing an objection regarding the mahr of a slave girl who is married with the master's permission and then freed. The objector argues that if intercourse occurs before emancipation, the master should receive only mahr al-mithl (the fair mahr for a slave), not the specified amount, since the vulva was his property. The Hanafi response, as conveyed by the author of al-Hidayah, is that the specified mahr (one thousand) is due, not mahr al-mithl, because the enforcement of the contract is retroactively attributed to the time of its conclusion. Although the contract was suspended pending the master's permission, when permission is granted, the contract is deemed effective from its inception. Thus, the specified mahr agreed upon at the time of the contract is valid. The subsequent ruling distinguishes: if she is freed after dukhul, the mahr goes to the master (since the vulva was his at the time of intercourse); if before dukhul, it goes to the woman. The passage draws an analogy to a suspended marriage (nikah mawquf) where a slave marries without permission and later gains it: the permission retroactively validates the contract from the beginning, so all acts of intercourse occur within a valid marriage, and only one mahr is due. The key principle is that nafadh (enforcement) is attributed to the time of the contract (wujud al-'aqd), which resolves any apparent conflict.

Key Terms
مہر (mahr): The dower given to the wife upon marriage; it can be specified (musamma) or fair (mithl).
مہر مثل (mahr al-mithl): The fair dower equivalent to what a woman of similar status receives; used when mahr is not specified or specification is invalid.
مہر سمی (mahr al-musamma): The dower specifically agreed upon by the parties at the time of marriage.
عقد موقوف (aqd mawquf): A suspended contract that is contingent upon permission of the master or guardian.
نفاذ (nafadh): Enforcement or execution of a contract; when a suspended contract is enforced, it is deemed effective from the time of conclusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a slave girl marries with the master's permission, specifying a mahr of 1000, and she is freed after dukhul, who receives the mahr?
A) The slave girl herself
B) The master
C) The husband
D) The mahr is split between master and woman

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi principle that enforcement (nafadh) is retroactive to the time of the contract ensures that the specified mahr is due in full, not mahr al-mithl, and its recipient depends on whether freedom occurs before or after consummation.

Father's Intercourse with Son's Slave-Girl: Umm Walad and Dispute with Zufar/Shafi'i
Explains ruling when father has child with son's slave-girl and disputes with Zufar/Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a father's intercourse with his son's slave-girl and explain the dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Zufar regarding ownership and mahr.

Core Idea
When necessity requires, ownership precedes intercourse—father pays value, not mahr, and she becomes umm walad.

This lesson examines a nuanced case in family law where a father's intercourse with his son's slave-girl leads to conflicting rulings between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i/Zufar position. The key lies in the temporal relationship between ownership and istilad (giving birth). We will unpack the Hanafi argument based on necessity and hadith, and then analyze the opposing view and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Summarize the Hanafi ruling: the father pays the value of the slave-girl (not mahr), she becomes his umm walad, and no mahr is due. This applies when the father claims lineage, is free, Muslim, and sane.
The ruling is based on the hadith 'Anta wa maluka li-abik' and the principle of necessity to avoid haram.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Zufar hold that the father must pay mahr (like a free woman) and she does not become umm walad because ownership is not established at the time of intercourse.
They analogize to a jointly owned slave-girl where even partial ownership triggers 'aqr.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Their proof: ownership is a ruling of istilad, so it comes after intercourse. Hence intercourse occurred in non-ownership, requiring mahr or 'aqr.
They cite the joint ownership case as a precedent for liability despite some ownership.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response distinguishes: here ownership is a condition (shart) for istilad, not a ruling. Necessity requires considering ownership prior to prevent the father's act from being haram. In joint ownership, partial ownership exists, so no such necessity arises.
The father's need for preservation of lineage is inferior to preservation of life, hence he pays value for the slave-girl but not for food.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical difference: Hanafi: father pays market value of the slave-girl and she becomes umm walad (free upon his death). Shafi'i/Zufar: father pays mahr (like a free woman) and she does not become umm walad.
The child's lineage and status also differ accordingly.

Source Text

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم كتاب النكاح ملک استیلا د سے پہلے ثابت ہوگی استیلاد کیلئے شرط ہو کر ۔ اسلئے کہ استیلاد کو بیچ کرنے والی حقیقت ملک ہے یا حق ملک اور باندی میں باپ کیلئے (ان میں سے ) کوئی بھی ثابت نہیں ہے۔ یہاں تک باپ کیلئے اپنے بیٹے کی باندی کے ساتھ نکاح جائز ہے۔ پس ضروری ہے ملک کو مقدم ماننا۔ پس ظاہر ہو گیا کہ وطی باپ کی ملک کے متصل ہے۔ لہذا باپ پر عقر لازم نہیں ہو گا۔ اور امام زفر اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ مہر واجب ہوگا ۔ کیونکہ یہ دونوں حضرات ملک کو استیلا کا حکم مان کر ثابت کرتے ہیں۔ جیسا کہ مشترکہ باندی میں۔ اورشی کا حکم شی ء کے بعد ہوتا ہے اور مسئلہ مشہور ہے۔
تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ باپ نے اپنے بیٹے کی باندی سے وطی کی۔ اس ولی کے نتیجہ میں باندی نے بچہ جنا تو یہ باندی باپ کی ام ولد کہلائے گی اور باپ پر اس باندی کی قیمت واجب ہوگی۔ اگر چہ باپ فقیر ہو اور بچہ کی قیمت واجب نہیں ہوگی ۔ البتہ باپ پر مہر واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ یہ باندی باپ کی ام ولد اس وقت ہوگی جب باپ اس بچہ کے نسب کا دعوی کرے کہ یہ بچہ میرے نطفہ سے ہے ۔ اور باپ آزاد مسلمان عاقل ہو۔ دلیل اسکی یہ ہے کہ باپ کو یہ ولایت حاصل ہے کہ وہ اپنے بیٹے کے مال کا مالک ہو جائے۔ اپنی جان کو باقی رکھنے کیلئے کیونکہ حدیث میں ہے انت و مالک لا بیک یعنی تو اور تیرا مال تیرے باپ کیلئے ہے۔ حضرت عائشہؓ سے روایت ہے ان رسول الله قال ولد الرجل من كسبه فكلوا من اموالهم يعنی آدمی کی اولا د اس کے کسب سے ہے پس ان کے اموال میں سے کھاؤ ۔ عمرو بن شعیب سے روایت ہے ان النبی صلى الله عليه وسلم قال ان اولاد کم من اطيب كسبكم فكلوا من كسب اولاد کم یعنی حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا تمہاری اولاد تمہاری بہترین کمائی ہے سوتم اپنی اولاد کی کمائی میں سے کھاؤ۔ اور ہر وہ شخص جس کے اپنے بیٹے کے مال کے مالک بننے کی ولایت حاصل ہے اپنے پانی کو محفوظ رکھنے کی وجہ سے۔
غيران الحاجة سے ایک اشکال کا جواب ہے۔ اشکال یہ ہے کہ اگر صیانت ماء بقاء نفس کے مانند ہے تو باپ پر باندی کی قیمت واجب نہ ہونی چاہئے۔ جیسا کہ کھانے پینے کی چیزوں میں باپ پر قیمت واجب نہیں ہوتی ۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے جواب میں فرمایا کہ بقاء نسل کی ضرورت بقاء نفس کی ضرورت سے کمتر ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ بیٹے کو اس پر مجبور نہیں کیا جائے گا کہ وہ باپ کو استیلاد کیلئے باندی دے۔
کیونکہ یہ غیر ضروری ہے۔ بس اس فرق کی وجہ سے باپ باندی کا مالک بالقیمۃ ہوگا۔ اور طعام کا بلا قیمت مالک ہوگا۔ ثم هذا الملك يثبت قبل الاستيلاد سے ایک اعتراض کا جواب ہے۔ حاصل اعتراض یہ ہے کہ استیلاد کیلئے ضروری ہے کہ وطی ملک میں کی گئی ہو۔ جیسا کہ مملوکہ باندی میں وطی کی گئی ہو جیسا کہ مکاتبہ باندی میں ۔ اور یہاں باپ کیلئے نہ حقیقت ملک ثبات ہے اور نہ حق ملک یہی وجہ ہے کہ بیٹے کی باندی کے ساتھ باپ کا نکاح جائز ہے۔ اگر بیٹے کی باندی میں باپ کیلئے حقیقت ملک یا حق ملک ہوتا تو اس کے ساتھ نکاح درست نہ ہوتا۔ بہر حال باپ کیلئے بیٹے کی باندی میں جب نہ حقیقت ملک ثابت ہے۔اور نہ حق ملک تو یہ باندی اس کی ام ولد کیسے ہو سکتی ہے۔ اور چونکہ غیر ملک میں دہلی کی گئی ہے لہذا باپ پر اس ولی کی وجہ سے عقر بھی واجب ہونا چاہئے تھا۔ جواب ضرورةً باپ کی ملک کو وطی پر مقدم مان لیا گیا ہے تا کہ باپ کا فعل حرام واقع نہ ہو۔ یا اسلئے کہ ملک صحت استیلا د کیلئے شرط ہے۔ اور شرط شی شی ء سے مقدم ہوتی ہے۔ پس جب شرط ہونے کی وجہ سے ملک وطی پر مقدم ہے تو یہ بات ظاہر ہو گئی کہ وطی باپ کی ملک میں واقع ہوئی ہے۔
اور جب ولی ملک میں پائی گئی تو باپ پر عقر بھی واجب نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مملوکہ کے ساتھ وطی کرنے سے عقر لازم نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ امام زفر اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اس صورت میں باپ پر مہر واجب ہوگا۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ دونوں بزرگ ملک کو استیلا کا حکم قرار دیتے ہیں۔ اور حکم شی شی ء کے بعد ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا باپ کی ملک ولی کے بعد ثابت ہوگی اور جب باپ کی ملک ولی کے بعد پائی گئی تو گویا باپ نے غیر مملوکہ باندی کے ساتھ وہلی کی ہے اور غیر مملوکہ کے ساتھ ولی کی صورت میں مہر اور عقر واجب ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا باپ پر اس وطی کی وجہ سے مہر واجب ہوگا۔ جیسا کہ مشترکہ باندی میں یعنی ایک باندی باپ اور بیٹے کے درمیان مشترک ہے پھر اس مشتر کہ باندی نے بچہ جنا باپ نے اس بچہ کے نسب کا دعوی کر دیا تو باپ سے اس بچہ کا نسب ثابت ہو گا ۔ اور باپ پر بالا جماع نصف عقر واجب ہوگا ۔ امام زفر اور امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ جاریہ مشتر کہ میں باپ کی ایک گونہ ملک قائم ہے۔ اسکے باوجود باپ پر عقر واجب کیا گیا ہے۔ پس جس صورت میں باپ کی ملک بالکل قائم نہیں ہے اس صورت میں باپ پر بدرجہ اولیٰ عقر واجب ہونا چاہئے ۔ ان حضرات کے قیاس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ مسئلہ مذکورہ میں ملک کو وطی پر مقدم مانا گیا ہے ضرورت کی وجہ سے تا کہ غیر ملک میں وطی واقع نہ ہو۔ اور اس مسئلہ میں چونکہ ایک گونہ ملک موجود ہے جو صحت استیلا دکیلئے کافی ہے اسلئے تقدیم ملک کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ یہ مسئلہ جامع صغیر کی شروح میں مشہور ہے کہ ہمارے نزدیک ملک استیلاد سے پہلے ثابت ہوگی شرط بن کر اور امام زفر اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک ملک استیلا د کے بعد حکم بن کر ثابت ہوگی۔ فائدہ عنقر ، آزاد عورتوں میں مہر شل ہوتا ہے اور باندی میں اگر باندی باکرہ ہے تو اس کی قیمت کا عشر عقر کہلائے گا اور اگر ثیبہ ہے تو اس کی قیمت کا نصف عشر عقر کہلائے گا۔ (فتح القدیر)
Ashraf al-Hidayah Urdu commentary on al-Hidayah, volume four, Kitab al-Nikah. Ownership is established before istilad (giving birth), as a condition for istilad. Because the reality that causes istilad is either actual ownership or a right of ownership, and neither is established for the father in the slave-girl. To the extent that marriage of the father with his son's slave-girl is permissible. So it is necessary to consider ownership as prior. Thus it becomes clear that intercourse is connected to the father's ownership. Therefore, 'aqr (compensation for intercourse) is not obligatory upon the father. Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i said that mahr is wajib, because these two consider ownership as the ruling of istilad, like in a jointly owned slave-girl. And the ruling of a thing comes after the thing, and the matter is well-known. Explanation: The scenario is that a father had intercourse with his son's slave-girl. As a result of this intercourse, the slave-girl gave birth. Then this slave-girl will be called umm walad of the father, and the father must pay her value, even if he is poor. However, he does not pay the child's value. But mahr is not obligatory upon the father. The author of al-Hidayah states that this slave-girl becomes umm walad for the father only when the father claims lineage of the child, i.e., this child is from my sperm, and the father is free, Muslim, and sane. The proof is that the father has the authority to own his son's property to preserve his own life, because in hadith it says: 'You and your property belong to your father.' It is narrated from Aisha: The Messenger of Allah said: 'A man's child is from his earnings, so eat from their wealth.' Amr ibn Shu'ayb narrated that the Prophet said: 'Your children are the best of your earnings, so eat from the earnings of your children.' And every person who has the authority to own his son's property because of preserving his sperm. 'Ghayran al-haja' is an answer to an objection. The objection is: If preservation of sperm is like preservation of life, then the father should not be liable for the price of the slave-girl, just as he is not liable for the price of food and drink. The author of al-Hidayah replied that the need for preservation of lineage is inferior to the need for preservation of life. That is why the son will not be compelled to give the father a slave-girl for istilad, because it is not necessary. So due to this difference, the father will own the slave-girl by price, and will own food without price. 'Thumma hadha al-mulk yathbutu qabla al-istilad' is an answer to another objection. The gist of the objection is that for istilad it is necessary that intercourse occur in ownership, as with a possessed slave-girl, as with a mukatabah slave-girl. And here the father has neither actual ownership nor right of ownership. That is why marriage of the father with the son's slave-girl is permissible. If the father had actual ownership or right of ownership in the son's slave-girl, his marriage with her would not be valid. In any case, when neither actual ownership nor right of ownership is established for the father in the son's slave-girl, how can she become his umm walad? And since intercourse occurred in non-ownership, therefore 'aqr should be wajib for that intercourse. The answer: By necessity, the father's ownership is considered prior to intercourse so that the father's act does not become haram, or because ownership is a condition for the validity of istilad, and a condition precedes the conditioned. So when ownership is prior to intercourse due to being a condition, it becomes clear that intercourse occurred in the father's ownership. And when intercourse occurred in ownership, 'aqr is not wajib, because intercourse with a possessed slave-girl does not necessitate 'aqr. Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i say that in this case mahr is wajib. Their proof: These two great scholars consider ownership as the ruling of istilad, and the ruling of a thing comes after the thing. Therefore, the father's ownership will be established after istilad. And when the father's ownership is found after istilad, it is as if the father had intercourse with a non-possessed slave-girl, and in the case of intercourse with a non-possessed slave-girl, mahr and 'aqr are wajib. So mahr is wajib for this intercourse, similar to a jointly owned slave-girl, i.e., a slave-girl shared between father and son. If that jointly owned slave-girl gives birth and the father claims lineage, the lineage is established from the father, and half 'aqr is wajib upon the father. Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i say: In a jointly owned slave-girl, the father has a kind of ownership, yet 'aqr is still wajib. So in the case where the father has no ownership at all, 'aqr should be more obviously wajib. The answer to their qiyas: In the mentioned case, ownership is considered prior to intercourse due to necessity, so that intercourse does not occur in non-ownership. In this case (joint ownership), since a kind of ownership exists sufficient for the validity of istilad, there is no need to prioritize ownership. This matter is well-known in the commentaries of al-Jami' al-Saghir: According to us, ownership is established before istilad as a condition; according to Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i, ownership is established after istilad as a ruling. Benefit: 'Aqr for free women is the mahr mithl; for a slave-girl, if she is a virgin, one-tenth of her value is called 'aqr; if she is non-virgin, half of one-tenth of her value is called 'aqr. (Fath al-Qadir)
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. It presents the Hanafi ruling: if a father has intercourse with his son's slave-girl and she gives birth, she becomes his umm walad, the father must pay her value but not the child's value, and no mahr is due. The father must claim lineage and be free, Muslim, and sane. The proof comes from hadith indicating a father's right to his son's property to preserve his own life and lineage. An objection arises: if preservation of sperm is like life, why must the father pay the value? The answer: preservation of lineage is a lesser need; hence the father owns the slave-girl by paying her value but not food. Another objection: intercourse in non-ownership should require 'aqr. The Hanafi response: ownership is considered prior by necessity to avoid haram; it is a condition that precedes the conditioned. Thus intercourse is deemed to occur in ownership, so no 'aqr. The dispute with Imam Zufar and Imam Shafi'i: they hold that ownership comes after istilad as a ruling, so the father's ownership is after intercourse; hence intercourse occurred in non-ownership, requiring mahr. They analogize to a jointly owned slave-girl, where even partial ownership triggers 'aqr. The Hanafi response distinguishes: in the father's own case, necessity requires prioritizing ownership completely; in joint ownership, since some ownership exists, no such necessity applies. The benefit note defines 'aqr for free women and slave-girls.

Key Terms
ام ولد (umm walad): A slave-girl who gives birth to her master's child; she becomes free upon his death and cannot be sold.
عقر ('aqr): Compensation for intercourse with a slave-girl not owned by the man; for free women it is mahr mithl, for slave-girls a fraction of value.
ملک (mulk): Ownership, particularly right of possession; here it refers to actual ownership or right of ownership over a slave-girl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, if a father has intercourse with his son's slave-girl and she gives birth, what is the father liable for?
A) He must pay both mahr and the value of the slave-girl.
B) He must pay only mahr, and the slave-girl becomes free.
C) He must pay the value of the slave-girl, but no mahr, and she becomes his umm walad.
D) He owes nothing because the intercourse was in non-ownership.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes ownership as a condition for istilad by necessity, leading to the father paying the slave-girl's value without mahr, contrary to Shafi'i/Zufar who treat ownership as a ruling of istilad.

Nikah — Marriage
intermediate
8 min
Son Marries His Slave-Girl to Father: No Umm Walad, Mahr Due, Child Free
Ruling with proof on validity and consequences of son marrying slave-girl to father

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a son marries his slave-girl to his father and she bears his child, and explain the proof based on complete ownership and shubha.

Core Idea
A son's complete ownership of his slave-girl prevents the father from any ownership; thus, no umm walad, mahr is due, child is free.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents a specific case: a son marries his own slave-girl to his father, and she gives birth. The ruling is nuanced and involves the interplay of ownership, marriage, and the concept of shubha. Understanding this ruling clarifies the boundaries between milk al-yamin and nikah, and highlights a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act: a son marries his slave-girl to his father; she gives birth. The ruling: the slave-girl does not become umm walad, the father owes mahr (not value), and the child is free.
The act involves marriage, not mere intercourse. The ruling is specific to this scenario.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof: the son owns the slave-girl 'from every aspect' (min kull wajh), so it is impossible for the father to own her simultaneously. This negates any fatherly ownership that would make her umm walad. The marriage protects the father's sperm, so milk al-yamin does not arise.
The dalil is a rational argument based on the nature of ownership.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The son's absolute ownership precludes any fatherly ownership. Therefore, the father's intercourse is protected by marriage (not ownership), so she does not become umm walad. The hadd for zina is dropped due to shubha (doubt in ownership).
Shubha arises because one might think the father has some right over the son's property, but this is not ownership.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Imam al-Shafi'i reportedly holds the marriage invalid, leading to different consequences: possibly no mahr, child status different, and maybe 'aqr (compensation for intercourse).
The Hanafi school holds the marriage valid because the slave-girl is not owned by the father.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi (operative for fatwa). The proof of absolute ownership is considered stronger, preventing any fatherly claim.
This ruling is from zahir al-riwayah.

قال ولو كان الابن زوجها اباه فولدت لم تصرام ولدله ولاقيمة عليه وعليه المهر وولدها حرلانه صح التزوج عندنا خلافا للشافعي لخلوها عن ملك الاب الايرى ان الابن ملكها من كل وجه فمن المحال ان يملكها الاب من وجه كذا يملك من التصرفات مالا يبقى معها ملك الاب لو كان فدل ذالك على انتفاء ملكه الاانه يسقط الحد للشبهة فاذاجاز النكاح صار ماؤه مصونابه فلم یثبت ملک الیمین فلاتصيرام ولدله ولاقيمة عليه فيها ولا فى ولدها لانه لم يملكهما وعليه المهر لالتزامه بالنكاح وولدها حرلانه ملكه اخوه فعتق عليه بالقرابة
ترجمہ اور اگر بیٹے نے اپنی باندی کا نکاح کیا اپنے باپ کے ساتھ پھر اس باندی نے اس باپ سے بچہ جنا تو وہ باندی باپ کی ام ولد نہیں ہوگی ۔ اور نہ باپ پر قیمت واجب ہوگی اور باپ پرمبر (واجب) ہوگا۔ اور اس باندی کا بچہ آزاد ہوگا۔ کیونکہ نکاح ہمارے نزدیک صحیح ہے۔ امام شافعی کا خلاف ہے باپ کی ملک سے باندی کے خالی ہونے کی وجہ سے۔ کیا نہیں دیکھتے کہ بیٹا باندی کا من کل وجہ مالک ہے۔ پس یہ بات محال ہے کہ باپ اس باندی کا من وجہ مالک ہو۔ اور اسی طرح بیٹا ایسے تصرفات کا مالک ہے جن کے ساتھ باپ کی ملک باقی نہ رہ سکتی۔ اگر ( ملک ) ہوتی تو یہ باپ کی ملک نہ ہونے پر دلالت کرتا ہے۔ لیکن حد زنا شبہ کی وجہ سے ساقط ہو جاتی ہے۔ پھر جب نکاح جائز ہو گیا تو باپ کا نطفہ محفوظ ہو گیا نکاح کی وجہ سے تو ملک یمین ثابت نہیں ہوتی لہذاوہ باپ کی ام ولد بھی نہیں ہوگی ۔ اور باپ پر قیمت (واجب) نہیں ہوگی نہ باندی میں اور نہ اس کی اولاد میں اسلئے کہ باپ دونوں کا مالک نہیں ہوا ہے۔ اور باپ پر مہبر (واجب) ہے اس کے
He said: And if the son married her (his slave-girl) to his father, and she gave birth, she does not become his (the father's) umm walad, and no value is due upon him, and upon him is the mahr, and her child is free, because the marriage is valid according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i, because she is devoid of the father's ownership. Do you not see that the son owns her from every aspect? So it is impossible that the father owns her from any aspect. Likewise, the son owns rights of disposal with which the father's ownership, if it existed, could not remain. This indicates the negation of his ownership. But the hadd (punishment for zina) is dropped due to the shubha (doubt). So when the marriage is valid, his sperm becomes protected (by the marriage), so milk al-yamin (ownership of the right hand) is not established. Thus she does not become his umm walad, and no value is due upon him, neither for her nor for her child, because he did not own them. And upon him is the mahr because of his commitment by the marriage. And her child is free because he is owned by his brother (the son), so he becomes free by kinship. Translation: And if the son married his slave-girl to his father, then that slave-girl gave birth to a child from that father, then that slave-girl will not become the father's umm walad, nor is the father liable for her value, and the father owes mahr, and that slave-girl's child is free. Because the marriage is valid according to us, contrary to al-Shafi'i, due to the slave-girl being devoid of the father's ownership. Do you not see that the son owns the slave-girl from every aspect? So it is impossible for the father to own her from any aspect. Similarly, the son owns such rights of disposal that the father's ownership could not remain with them if it existed. This indicates the negation of his ownership. But the hadd for zina is dropped due to shubha. Then when the marriage became valid, the father's sperm became protected by the marriage, so milk al-yamin is not established. Therefore she does not become his umm walad. And no value is due upon the father, neither for her nor for her child, because the father did not own them. And upon the father is the mahr because of his commitment by the marriage. And her child is free because he is owned by his brother (the son), so he becomes free by kinship.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It addresses the case where the son marries his own slave-girl to his father. The father has intercourse with her through the marriage, she gives birth. The ruling: she does NOT become the father's umm walad; the father owes the mahr (not the value); the child is free. The proof: The son fully owns the slave-girl, so it is impossible for the father to have any ownership in her simultaneously. The marriage is valid because the slave-girl is not owned by the father; thus the father's sperm is protected by marriage, not by ownership of the right hand. Therefore, milk al-yamin (ownership that would make her umm walad) is not established. The father is not liable for her value because he never owned her. He is liable for mahr because he contracted marriage, which entails mahr. The child is free because the child is owned by his brother (the son), and the son's ownership over his brother results in freedom by kinship (the son cannot own his brother). The hadd for zina is dropped due to shubha (doubt in ownership). The dispute with al-Shafi'i is noted: al-Shafi'i may consider the marriage invalid because the father has some right over his son's property, but here the marriage is valid because the son's ownership is complete and the father has no ownership in her.

Key Terms
ملک یمین (milk al-yamin): Ownership by right of the right hand; i.e., ownership of a slave; here it is the basis for umm walad status.
شبہ (shubha): Doubt or ambiguity that prevents application of hadd (punishment) for zina; here the doubtful ownership of the father.
نطفہ (nutfah): Sperm; here 'his sperm becomes protected' meaning lineage is established through marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a son marries his slave-girl to his father and she gives birth to a child, what is the father's liability according to the Hanafi school?
A) He must pay the value of the slave-girl and she becomes his umm walad.
B) He owes only the mahr, and the child is free.
C) He owes nothing because the marriage is invalid.
D) He must pay both mahr and the value of the child.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a son's complete ownership of his slave-girl prevents the father from acquiring any ownership, so no umm walad status arises, but the father owes mahr and the child is free.
